Uthman's Modesty as Fruit of Certainty
A causal chain linking Uthman's modesty to inner certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Uthman's modesty (hayā') before Allah is a direct fruit of perfect knowledge (ma'rifa) and firm certainty (yaqīn), manifested through vigilance (murāqaba) and culminating in a state akin to direct vision (mu'āyana).

Core Idea
Uthman's modesty is not shyness; it blooms from inward certainty.

This lesson examines a brief but profound passage from Imam al-Sanūsī that links outward behavior to inward spiritual states. By reflecting on the character of ‘Uthmān ibn ‘Affān (RA), we see how perfect knowledge and certainty produce a life of divine vigilance. The passage shows that true modesty before Allah is the fruit of a heart that lives in constant awareness of Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the compact style.
2
Identify the chain of spiritual causes
Trace the sequence: modesty (hayā') ← vigilance (murāqaba) ← perfect knowledge and firm certainty (kamāl al-ma'rifa wa rusūkh al-yaqīn).
The author explicitly uses 'thamar' (fruit) twice.
3
Understand the phrase 'as if seeing'
Reflect on the term ka-annahu mu'āyana — a state where certainty becomes so strong it is like direct vision. How does this connect to modesty?
This is the pinnacle of the chain.
4
Reflect on personal application
Ask yourself: How can I cultivate vigilance (murāqaba) in my own life to increase my sense of Allah's presence?
This is a practical takeaway from the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ في عثمان رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : « إِنَّهُ لَتَسْتَحْيِي مِنْهُ مَلَائِكَةُ السَّمَاءِ » ورُوِيَ : أنَّه لم يكن يرفع رأسَهُ إلى السماءِ حياءً مِنَ اللهِ ؛ وذلك ثمرة المراقبة التي هي ثمرة كمال المعرفة ورسوخ اليقين ، حتى كأنَّهُ معاينة .
And he ﷺ said concerning Uthman - may Allah be pleased with him: 'Indeed, the angels of heaven are shy of him.' And it is narrated that he would not raise his head to the sky out of modesty from Allah. And that is the fruit of vigilance (muraqaba) which is the fruit of perfect knowledge and firm certainty, until he is as if seeing (with direct vision).
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage defines the station of Uthman by quoting a hadith that angels are shy of him and a report that he never raised his head to the sky out of hayā' (modesty) from Allah. The author then explains that this behavior is the fruit of muraqaba, which itself is the fruit of kamāl al-ma'rifa (perfect knowledge) and rusūkh al-yaqin (firm certainty), to the point that he was as if he were seeing Allah with direct vision (mu'āyana). Thus the outward action (modesty) is traced back to its inward cause (certainty).

Key Terms
مراقبة
معرفة
يقين
معاينة
حياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's modesty was merely shyness or a personality trait.
Correction: The passage explains that his modesty was the fruit of perfect knowledge and firm certainty, not mere shyness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the immediate result of perfect knowledge and firm certainty?
A) Shyness of angels.
B) Muraqaba (vigilance).
C) Mu'āyana (seeing directly).
D) Not raising the head.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's modesty is the visible fruit of his inner certainty and constant awareness of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are alone and no one sees you, does your head lower in modesty before Allah, or do you feel free to do as you please? What would your level of haya' in private reveal about the depth of your certainty?
?
You claim to know Allah, but does your outward behavior—especially in moments of trial—reflect the vigilance (muraqaba) that comes from perfect knowledge? If not, what is the gap between what you know and how you live?
?
The angels were shy of Uthman because his modesty was rooted in certainty so strong it was as if he saw Allah. If the angels observed your state of faith today, would they shy away from you out of reverence, or would they pity your neglect? What must change in your daily awareness to make that truth real in your life?

Abu Bakr's Unshakable Certainty
Hadith about Abu Bakr's certainty at its peak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith indicating that Abu Bakr's certainty was already at its peak, such that even supernatural unveiling would not increase it.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's certainty was already complete — no veil could add to it.

The author begins by presenting a powerful hadith about Abu Bakr's faith. This tradition highlights the unique level of certainty (yaqin) that Abu Bakr possessed. Let's examine its meaning and implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic and translation of the hadith about Abu Bakr's certainty. Note the conditional phrase 'if the veil were removed' and the result 'his certainty would not increase.'
The veil refers to supernatural mysteries that are hidden from ordinary perception.
2
Understand the meaning of 'unshakable certainty'
Reflect on why certainty that cannot increase is considered the highest level. What does this tell us about Abu Bakr's faith?
This hadith places Abu Bakr at the pinnacle of certainty among the Companions.
3
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this hadith supports the author's argument about the Companions' virtues. Abu Bakr's certainty is presented as evidence of his excellence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أبي بكرٍ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : « لَوْ كُشِفَ الْغِطَاءُ عَنْ أَبِي بَكْرٍ .. مَا أَزْدَادَ يَقِيناً » وقالَ : « مَا فَضَلَكُمْ أَبُو بَكْرٍ بِكَثِيرِ صَلَاةٍ وَلَا صِيَامٍ ، وَإِنَّمَا فَضَلَكُمْ بِشَيْءٍ وَقَرَ فِي قَلْبِهِ » ورُوِيَ : أنَّ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ سأل جبريل عليه السلام عن فضائل عمر رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ ، فقالَ : « لَوْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ مَا لَبِثَ نُوحٌ فِي قَوْمِهِ : أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِينَ عَاماً .. مَا وَفَّيْتُ بِفَضَائِل عُمَرَ ، وَإِنَّهُ حَسَنَةٌ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ » وما عسى أنْ أعدَّ مِنْ محاسنِ الصحابة ومآثرهم ؟! ويكفي في رسوخ معارفهم وقُوَّةِ إيمانِهم قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَأَلْزَمَهُمْ كَلِمَةَ التَّقْوَى وَكَانُوا أَحَقَّ بِهَا وَأَهْلَهَا ﴾ [الفتح : ٢٦]
And the Prophet ﷺ said concerning Abu Bakr - may Allah be pleased with him: 'If the veil were removed from Abu Bakr, his certainty would not increase.' And he said: 'Abu Bakr did not surpass you by much prayer or fasting, but he surpassed you by something that settled in his heart.' And it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ asked Jibril - peace be upon him - about the virtues of Umar - may Allah be pleased with him. He said: 'If I remained among you as long as Noah remained among his people: one thousand years less fifty years, I would not do justice to the virtues of Umar. And indeed, he is one good deed of the good deeds of Abu Bakr.' And how much can I count of the good qualities and achievements of the Companions? Sufficient for the firmness of their knowledge and the strength of their faith is the saying of the Exalted: 'And He made them adhere to the word of taqwa, and they were most deserving of it and its people' (Quran 48:26).
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage provides further evidence of the Companions' certainty, focusing on Abu Bakr and linking Umar's virtue to him. It begins with the famous hadith that even if the supernatural veil were lifted, Abu Bakr's certainty would not increase because it was already at the peak. The second hadith explains that Abu Bakr's superiority was not due to excessive worship but due to an inner conviction (wara) fixed in his heart. The author then cites a narration where Jibril tells the Prophet that Umar's virtues are so vast that even Noah's long stay could not exhaust them, and crucially, Umar is described as 'one good deed from the good deeds of Abu Bakr,' highlighting Abu Bakr's supreme status. The passage concludes by stating that the firm knowledge and strong faith of all the Companions is sufficiently attested by the Quranic verse that Allah made them adhere to the kalimat al-taqwa (word of piety), and they were most deserving of it.

Key Terms
يقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Abu Bakr's certainty was less than that of the prophets or could grow with supernatural unveiling.
Correction: The hadith explicitly says his certainty would not increase even if the veil were removed, indicating it was already at its peak, comparable to prophetic certainty.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith say about Abu Bakr's certainty if the veil were removed?
A) It would increase greatly.
B) It would not increase.
C) It would become like that of the prophets.
D) It would be revealed as weak.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's certainty was already so complete that even supernatural unveiling could not add to it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Bakr's certainty was so complete that even seeing the unseen would not add to it. How does your own certainty compare? Are there areas of your faith where you still need 'proof' or 'unveiling' to believe? What does that reveal about the strength of your iman? Commit today to one step to increase your certainty through the means that are available: studying the Qur'an, reflecting on creation, or seeking knowledge.
?
If the veil were lifted for you right now, would your certainty increase? Why? What is holding you back from having that level of certainty now? Write a sincere dua asking Allah to grant you the same yaqin that He granted Abu Bakr.
?
The hadith implies that Abu Bakr's certainty was already at the pinnacle. In light of this, what can you do to remove the veils of doubt and distraction in your own heart? Are you actively seeking certainty, or are you satisfied with uncertainty? Pledge to take one concrete action today to strengthen your faith.

The Secret of Abu Bakr's Excellence
Hadith explaining Abu Bakr's superiority is due to an inner quality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Abu Bakr surpassed other Companions not by outward worship but by an inner spiritual quality settled in his heart.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's superiority was due to an inner conviction, not outward deeds.

The second hadith explains the true basis of Abu Bakr's excellence. It corrects the misconception that his superiority was due to more prayer or fasting. Instead, it points to a profound inner quality.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith about Abu Bakr's superiority
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the negation: 'not by much prayer or fasting.' Then the affirmation: 'by something settled in his heart.'
This 'something' is often interpreted as deep ma'rifa (gnosis) or ikhlas (sincerity).
2
Reflect on the meaning of 'something settled in his heart'
What could this quality be? Consider terms like yaqin, ihsan, or mahabbah. How does this align with the earlier hadith about his certainty?
The phrase 'wara' in the commentary suggests an inner piety or scrupulousness.
3
Connect to the broader theme of inner vs outer faith
This hadith emphasizes that true excellence in the sight of Allah is a matter of the heart, not just outward actions. Why is this important in theology?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أبي بكرٍ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : « لَوْ كُشِفَ الْغِطَاءُ عَنْ أَبِي بَكْرٍ .. مَا أَزْدَادَ يَقِيناً » وقالَ : « مَا فَضَلَكُمْ أَبُو بَكْرٍ بِكَثِيرِ صَلَاةٍ وَلَا صِيَامٍ ، وَإِنَّمَا فَضَلَكُمْ بِشَيْءٍ وَقَرَ فِي قَلْبِهِ » ورُوِيَ : أنَّ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ سأل جبريل عليه السلام عن فضائل عمر رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ ، فقالَ : « لَوْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ مَا لَبِثَ نُوحٌ فِي قَوْمِهِ : أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِينَ عَاماً .. مَا وَفَّيْتُ بِفَضَائِل عُمَرَ ، وَإِنَّهُ حَسَنَةٌ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ » وما عسى أنْ أعدَّ مِنْ محاسنِ الصحابة ومآثرهم ؟! ويكفي في رسوخ معارفهم وقُوَّةِ إيمانِهم قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَأَلْزَمَهُمْ كَلِمَةَ التَّقْوَى وَكَانُوا أَحَقَّ بِهَا وَأَهْلَهَا ﴾ [الفتح : ٢٦]
And the Prophet ﷺ said concerning Abu Bakr - may Allah be pleased with him: 'If the veil were removed from Abu Bakr, his certainty would not increase.' And he said: 'Abu Bakr did not surpass you by much prayer or fasting, but he surpassed you by something that settled in his heart.' And it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ asked Jibril - peace be upon him - about the virtues of Umar - may Allah be pleased with him. He said: 'If I remained among you as long as Noah remained among his people: one thousand years less fifty years, I would not do justice to the virtues of Umar. And indeed, he is one good deed of the good deeds of Abu Bakr.' And how much can I count of the good qualities and achievements of the Companions? Sufficient for the firmness of their knowledge and the strength of their faith is the saying of the Exalted: 'And He made them adhere to the word of taqwa, and they were most deserving of it and its people' (Quran 48:26).
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage provides further evidence of the Companions' certainty, focusing on Abu Bakr and linking Umar's virtue to him. It begins with the famous hadith that even if the supernatural veil were lifted, Abu Bakr's certainty would not increase because it was already at the peak. The second hadith explains that Abu Bakr's superiority was not due to excessive worship but due to an inner conviction (wara) fixed in his heart. The author then cites a narration where Jibril tells the Prophet that Umar's virtues are so vast that even Noah's long stay could not exhaust them, and crucially, Umar is described as 'one good deed from the good deeds of Abu Bakr,' highlighting Abu Bakr's supreme status. The passage concludes by stating that the firm knowledge and strong faith of all the Companions is sufficiently attested by the Quranic verse that Allah made them adhere to the kalimat al-taqwa (word of piety), and they were most deserving of it.

Key Terms
قلب

Checkpoint

A) Because of his long prayers.
B) Because of his frequent fasting.
C) Because of both prayer and fasting.
D) Because of something settled in his heart.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's superiority was due to an inner spiritual quality, not mere outward worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is that 'something' in your heart that truly defines your faith? Does it outweigh your outward acts of worship, or do you rely on your deeds?
?
If your prayers and fasting were stripped away, what would remain in your heart that Allah values? Is it enough?
?
Abu Bakr's excellence was not due to much prayer or fasting. Are you content with your outward worship, or are you cultivating the inner quality that settles in the heart?

Umar's Virtues and Abu Bakr's Supremacy
Narration about Umar's virtues and their connection to Abu Bakr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the narration linking Umar's vast virtues to Abu Bakr's merit, and how it underscores Abu Bakr's supreme rank.

Core Idea
Umar's virtues are so extensive that even Noah's lifespan could not do them justice, yet they are but a single good deed of Abu Bakr.

The author now presents a remarkable narration where Jibril describes Umar's virtues to the Prophet. The hyperbolic comparison to Noah's long mission emphasizes their greatness, and the final clause ties all this virtue back to Abu Bakr.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration about Umar and Jibril
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: Jibril says even if the Prophet stayed as long as Noah (950 years), he couldn't exhaust Umar's virtues.
This is a hadith by some accounts, but its chain may be weak; the author uses it to illustrate a point.
2
Understand the final phrase: 'he is one good deed of Abu Bakr'
This connects Umar's virtues to Abu Bakr, indicating that even the great Umar is a product of Abu Bakr's merit. Reflect on the implication for Abu Bakr's status.
Some interpret this as Umar being a 'good deed' of Abu Bakr on the Day of Judgment, highlighting Abu Bakr's intercession or influence.
3
Reflect on the theology of companionship
This narration reinforces the hierarchy among the Companions and the unique position of Abu Bakr. How does this align with Sunni beliefs about the khulafa?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أبي بكرٍ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : « لَوْ كُشِفَ الْغِطَاءُ عَنْ أَبِي بَكْرٍ .. مَا أَزْدَادَ يَقِيناً » وقالَ : « مَا فَضَلَكُمْ أَبُو بَكْرٍ بِكَثِيرِ صَلَاةٍ وَلَا صِيَامٍ ، وَإِنَّمَا فَضَلَكُمْ بِشَيْءٍ وَقَرَ فِي قَلْبِهِ » ورُوِيَ : أنَّ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ سأل جبريل عليه السلام عن فضائل عمر رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ ، فقالَ : « لَوْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ مَا لَبِثَ نُوحٌ فِي قَوْمِهِ : أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِينَ عَاماً .. مَا وَفَّيْتُ بِفَضَائِل عُمَرَ ، وَإِنَّهُ حَسَنَةٌ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ » وما عسى أنْ أعدَّ مِنْ محاسنِ الصحابة ومآثرهم ؟! ويكفي في رسوخ معارفهم وقُوَّةِ إيمانِهم قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَأَلْزَمَهُمْ كَلِمَةَ التَّقْوَى وَكَانُوا أَحَقَّ بِهَا وَأَهْلَهَا ﴾ [الفتح : ٢٦]
And the Prophet ﷺ said concerning Abu Bakr - may Allah be pleased with him: 'If the veil were removed from Abu Bakr, his certainty would not increase.' And he said: 'Abu Bakr did not surpass you by much prayer or fasting, but he surpassed you by something that settled in his heart.' And it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ asked Jibril - peace be upon him - about the virtues of Umar - may Allah be pleased with him. He said: 'If I remained among you as long as Noah remained among his people: one thousand years less fifty years, I would not do justice to the virtues of Umar. And indeed, he is one good deed of the good deeds of Abu Bakr.' And how much can I count of the good qualities and achievements of the Companions? Sufficient for the firmness of their knowledge and the strength of their faith is the saying of the Exalted: 'And He made them adhere to the word of taqwa, and they were most deserving of it and its people' (Quran 48:26).

The passage concludes by stating that the firm knowledge and strong faith of all the Companions is sufficiently attested by the Quranic verse that Allah made them adhere to the kalimat al-taqwa (word of piety), and they were most deserving of it.

The Companions' Firm Knowledge and Faith
Quranic verse as proof of the Companions' faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verse (48:26) serves as sufficient proof of the Companions' deep knowledge and strong faith.

Core Idea
The Quran itself testifies to the Companions' firmness in taqwa and their being its rightful people.

The author concludes this section by invoking a powerful Quranic verse. Instead of enumerating all the virtues of the Companions, he declares that one verse suffices to establish the depth of their knowledge and faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and its placement
Read the Arabic of the verse (al-Fath 48:26) and the translation. Note how the author uses it as a proof: 'يكفي في رسوخ معارفهم وقوة إيمانهم'.
The verse refers to the treaty of Hudaybiyyah context, but the author applies it generally.
2
Understand the meaning of 'kalimat al-taqwa'
What is the 'word of taqwa'? Scholars interpret it as the declaration of tawhid or the Quranic guidance. The Companions were made to adhere to it.
Taqwa means piety, God-consciousness.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'they were most deserving of it'
This indicates that the Companions were the rightful bearers of this word. What does that imply about their status?
It shows their unique merit and suitability for carrying the message.

The Weakness of the Muqallid's Faith and Its Vulnerability to Doubts
Sanusi warns that the faith of the muqallid is weak and prone to collapse when doubts arise, especially at death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the faith of a muqallid (blind follower) is vulnerable to doubts and calamities, and why certain knowledge based on proofs is necessary.

Core Idea
Blind faith cannot withstand the grave's tests.

Sanusi now turns to a practical consequence of taqlid: its fragility. He warns that a faith not rooted in decisive evidence is at risk of collapsing when serious doubts or trials arise—especially the trials of the grave. This passage challenges those who think simply believing without understanding is enough.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the specific terms: 'shalat' (fall/sprain) and 'dawahi' (calamities).
2
Identify the three requirements for firm faith
The passage lists three things: a statement established by evidences, strength of certainty, and a firm contract that does not shake. Understand each.
3
Connect to why taqlid fails
Reflect on why the muqallid lacks these three and how that leads to vulnerability at death.
The muqallid's faith is not built on decisive proofs, so it lacks the necessary strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُخشى على صاحبها الشلتُ عند عروض الشبهات ، ونزول الدواهي المعضلاتِ ؛ كالقبر ونحوه ، مما يفتقرُ إلى قول ثابت بالأدلَّةِ وقُوَّةِ يقينٍ وعَقْدٍ راسخ لا يتزلزل ؛ لكونه نُتِجَ عن قواطع البراهين
And one fears for its owner the fall (shalat) at the occurrence of doubts and the descent of grievous calamities — like the grave and similar to it — which require a statement established by evidences, and a strength of certainty, and a firm contract that does not shake, because it is produced by decisive proofs.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a warning about the faith of the muqallid (one who follows blindly without proof). The author states that such a person is at risk of falling (shalat) when faced with doubts and great trials, such as the calamities of the grave and similar severe tests. These situations require a faith that is established by proofs (adilla), with strength of certainty (quwwat yaqin), and a firm covenant (aqd raskh) that does not waver. The reason: such firm faith is the product of decisive proofs (qawati' al-barahin). Thus, taqlid alone is insufficient to withstand the severe trials of the afterlife. The implication is that believers must strive to acquire certain knowledge of their faith through proofs, not rely solely on imitation.

الشبهات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: This passage shows that blind faith is weak and may not survive major trials like the grave; only faith based on decisive proofs is firm.

Key Takeaway
The faith of a muqallid (blind follower) is weak and may collapse under trials like the grave because it is not built on decisive proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage describes faith as needing 'a statement established by evidences, strength of certainty, and a firm contract that does not shake.' Which of these three do you feel weakest in, and how can you actively develop it starting tomorrow?
?
Are you willing to risk your salvation on a faith that may collapse when doubts or calamities come? What is one concrete action you will take today to build the kind of faith that 'does not shake'?

The Vulnerability of Blind Faith
Sanusi warns that a muqallid's faith may collapse under trial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the faith of a muqallid is considered weak and how it differs from faith based on certain knowledge and evidence.

Core Idea
Faith without evidence is fragile; only decisive proofs yield unwavering certainty.

Sanusi now turns to a practical warning: not all faith is equal in its resilience. While the previous sections established the necessity of knowledge, this passage explains why faith based on mere imitation (taqlid) is dangerously fragile. When trials come—especially the trial of the grave—only a conviction built on solid evidence can stand firm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the passage carefully. The heading states the problem: weakness and vulnerability. Notice what Sanusi says about the owner of taqlid—what is feared for them?
The word 'الشلتُ' may be a typo for 'الزلل' (slip) or 'الزوال' (removal).
2
Understand the trials mentioned
Sanusi mentions two types of trials: doubts that arise, and calamitous difficulties—especially the grave. Why is the grave singled out? Reflect on its significance.
3
Contrast with firm faith
The passage describes what true faith requires: statements grounded in evidence, strength of certainty, and a firm contract that does not waver. How does this contrast with taqlid?
The decisive proofs (qawati' al-barahin) are the source of this firmness.
4
Identify the core lesson
The conclusion is that faith must be produced by proof, not inherited. Why does Sanusi emphasize this? Consider the purpose of Ilm al-Kalam.
This passage is a direct argument for the necessity of acquiring theological proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ضعف إيمان المقلد وعرضته للشك والزوال] ويُخشى على صاحبها الشلتُ عند عروض الشبهات ، ونزول الدواهي المعضلاتِ ؛ كالقبر ونحوه ، مما يفتقر إلى قول ثابت بالأدلَّةِ وقُوَّةِ يقينٍ وعَقْدِ راسخ لا يتزلزل ؛ لكونه نُتِجَ عن قواطع البراهينِ
[The weakness of the faith of the follower and its exposure to doubt and removal] And it is feared for its owner—[i.e., the practice of taqlid]—that he may slip when doubts arise and when calamitous difficulties descend, like the grave and similar, which require a statement established by evidences, and strength of certainty, and a firm contract that does not waver, because it is produced by decisive proofs.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a warning about the danger of taqlid (blind imitation) in matters of faith. The heading states the topic: the weakness of the muqallid's faith and its exposure to doubt and eventual loss. Sanusi explains that the follower (sahib al-taqlid) is feared to slip (yukhsha 'alayhi al-zalal) when doubts (shubuhat) occur and when severe trials descend upon him—especially the trial of the grave (al-qabr) and similar moments of crisis. Such trials require a statement (qawl) firmly grounded in evidences (adilla), strength of certainty (quwwat yaqin), and a firm resolve ('aqd rasikh) that does not shake. This firmness can only come from faith that is produced (nutija) by conclusive proofs (qawati' al-barahin). The underlying message is that mere inherited faith, without personal intellectual conviction, is fragile and prone to collapse when faced with serious doubts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Being born into a Muslim family is sufficient for salvation regardless of one's level of conviction.
Correction: This passage shows that personal conviction based on proof is essential, because inherited faith without evidence is weak and may collapse during trials like the grave.

Checkpoint

C) Knowledge of Arabic
D) Following a particular school of law

Key Takeaway
The faith of a muqallid is weak because it lacks the firm foundation of certain knowledge produced by decisive proofs, making it prone to collapse when doubts and trials arise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
What specific, concrete steps have you taken to build a 'firm contract' with Allah that cannot waver? Or have you assumed that simply being Muslim is enough to survive the tests ahead?

Two Types of Hypocrisy and the Necessity of Self-Reflection
Sanusi distinguishes two kinds of nifaq and emphasizes knowing oneself to know Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two types of hypocrisy as defined by Sanusi, why blind imitation (taqlid) leads to hidden hypocrisy, and why self-reflection is essential for salvation from the trial of the grave.

Core Idea
Blind imitation without self-reflection is a hidden form of hypocrisy.

Sanusi warns that the trial of the grave can only be overcome by those who base their faith on proof and reflection, not on blind imitation. He then reveals a profound insight: there are two kinds of hypocrisy, one conscious and one unconscious. The unconscious kind is especially dangerous because the person does not even realize they are a hypocrite. This passage calls us to examine ourselves and abandon mere custom in favor of genuine conviction through reflection (nazar).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author’s flow and key terms sink in.
Pay attention to the words 'نفاق', 'تقليد', and 'نظر'.
2
Identify the two types of hypocrisy
Locate where the author cites the saying that hypocrisy is of two kinds. Notice how he distinguishes them: one known to the person, the other unknown.
The first type is the conscious hypocrisy of the Prophet's era; the second is unconscious imitation.
3
Understand why the second type is dangerous
Reflect on the example of a person born to Muslim parents who merely repeats the shahada without thought. This person would have believed similarly if born elsewhere. This reveals that faith without reflection is not true faith.
4
Connect to the devilish whisper and the way out
Notice how the author ends with the prophetic saying about knowing oneself, and the warning that a devil may discourage reflection. Ask yourself: how does this apply to me?
The solution is to engage in nazar despite whispers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : هذه الفتنةُ فتنة القبر لا ينجو منها مَنْ أخذ في دينه بالتقليد وترك النظر في أدلَّةِ الرسالة والتوحيد ، ولذلك قيل : النفاق نفاقانِ : نفاق يعرفُهُ صاحبُهُ مِنْ نفسِهِ ؛ وهو نفاقُ الذين كانوا في عهد النبي صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، ومَنْ في معناهم مِنَ الزنادقة ، ونفاق لا يعرفُهُ صاحبُهُ مِنْ نفسِهِ ؛ وهو أنْ يُولَدَ الرجلُ أو المرأةُ بينَ أبوين مسلمين ، فيسمع قول : لا إله إلا الله ، محمَّدٌ رسولُ اللهِ ، فيقول نحو ما سمع اتباعاً وتقليداً لهم ، حتى لو تُصُوِّرَ أنْ يُولَدَ بين النصارى لَقَالَ مثل أقوالهم اتباعاً لهم وتقليداً في ذلكَ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ ينظر في خلقِهِ ، ومِنْ أي شيءٍ خُلِقَ ، وكيفَ انتقلَ مِنْ طَورٍ إلى طورٍ ، ولذلك قال عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : « مَنْ عَرَفَ نَفْسَهُ عَرَفَ رَبَّهُ » وربَّما يمرُّ بباله الفكرُ في خَلْقِ اللهِ ، فيردُّه شيطانُ مِنَ الإِنسِ أَوِ الجنّ ، فيقولُ لهُ : إِنْ تَفَكَّرتَ فقد تشكَّكْتَ ، فيُعْرِضُ عَنِ النظر
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: This trial – the trial of the grave – none will be saved from it except those who take (taqlid) in their religion and abandon reflection on the proofs of the message and tawhid. Therefore it was said: Hypocrisy is of two kinds: hypocrisy that its owner knows from himself; this is the hypocrisy of those who were in the era of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) and those like them among the heretics; and hypocrisy that its owner does not know from himself; this is when a man or a woman is born between two Muslim parents, and he hears the statement: There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and he says something like what he heard out of following and taqlid of them, such that if it were imagined that he were born among Christians, he would have said similar to their statements out of following and taqlid of them in that, without reflecting on his own creation, from what he was created, and how he progressed from stage to stage. For that reason he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Whoever knows himself knows his Lord.' And perhaps the thought about the creation of Allah passes through his mind, but a devil from among humans or jinn repels him, saying to him: 'If you reflect, you will become doubtful,' so he turns away from reflection.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a classification and warning. The author begins by stating that no one will be saved from the trial of the grave except those who take their religion by proof and reflect on the proofs of prophethood and tawhid. Those who blindly follow (taqlid) are doomed. Then he cites a statement: 'Hypocrisy is of two kinds.' The first kind is known to the person himself—the hypocrisy of those who outwardly profess Islam while inwardly disbelieving, like the hypocrites of the Prophet's time and similar heretics. The second kind is hypocrisy that the person himself does not recognize. This occurs when someone is born to Muslim parents and simply repeats the shahada out of imitation and taqlid, without any personal reflection or conviction. If such a person were born to Christian parents, he would similarly repeat their statements. He does not reflect on his own creation, his origin, or his development from stage to stage. The author then quotes the famous saying (attributed to the Prophet but actually a saying of the early scholar Yahya ibn Mu'adh): 'Whoever knows himself knows his Lord.' This indicates that self-reflection leads to knowledge of the Creator. Finally, the author warns that when a thought about Allah's creation occurs to such a person, a devil (human or jinn) may repel him, saying: 'If you reflect, you will fall into doubt.' So he turns away from reflection. Thus, the passage teaches that hidden hypocrisy is born from sheer imitation without thought, and the only escape is to engage in reflection (nazar) despite Satanic whispers.

تقليد
نظر
معرفة النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that hypocrisy is always a deliberate, conscious act of deception.
Correction: Sanusi explains that there is a hidden hypocrisy where a person believes they are Muslim but their faith is only imitation, not conviction, and they would have followed any religion they were born into.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what characterizes the second type of hypocrisy that the person does not know about himself?
A) Deliberately hiding disbelief.
B) Born among Muslims, hears and repeats the shahada without reflection.
C) Rejecting the prophets.
D) Denying the resurrection.

Key Takeaway
True faith requires personal reflection (nazar) on one's own existence and the proofs of revelation, not blind imitation (taqlid), which can lead to hidden hypocrisy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to imagine yourself born into a non-Muslim family, would your beliefs today be essentially the same as your family's, or have you truly examined the foundations of your faith for yourself? What would you say to your Creator if He asked you why you believed?
?
When a thought about the beginning of your existence or the intricacy of your creation crosses your mind, do you silence it out of a vague fear of doubt? Could that very fear be a whisper of the devil, turning you away from the very path that leads to knowing your Lord?
?
If the trial of the grave were to confront you tonight, could you honestly say your faith is built on proof and reflection, or are you relying on the imitation of those around you? What concrete step will you take this week to move from taqlid to nazar?

Faith and Disbelief

Refutation of the Claim that No Believer is a Blind Follower
Sanusi refutes the claim that no believer is a blind follower and that all have certain knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's refutation of the claim that all believers have certain knowledge without reflection, and why reflection (nazar) is necessary for many beliefs.

Core Idea
Faith does not automatically grant certain knowledge; some beliefs require evidence and reflection.

Sanusi tackles a claim that seems pious but undermines the very purpose of theological reasoning. Some contemporaries argued that every believer possesses certain knowledge of faith, differing only in expression. Sanusi shows why this view is not only weaker than previous erroneous positions but also leads to absurd consequences, such as rendering God's commands to reflect pointless.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Read the beginning of the passage to understand what Sanusi is responding to: the assertion that there is no blind follower among believers, and that all have knowledge.
Notice that Sanusi calls this saying even weaker than a previous Indian view.
2
Follow Sanusi's arguments
The passage lists several reasons why this claim is false: the need for precise reflection, the historical sectarian divisions, the prophetic hadith about 73 sects, and the absurdity of commanding what is already obtained.
Each argument stands on its own; try to see how they connect.
3
Reflect on the role of evidence
Consider why Sanusi emphasizes that beliefs like oneness and resurrection require proofs from the Quran. This shows that faith is not blind but based on reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولُ مَنْ قالَ : لا مُقلد في المؤمنينَ وأضعفُ مِنْ هذا : قولُ بعض المعاصرين : لا مُقلد المؤمنينَ عامهم وخاصهم ، وإنَّ جميعهم حصلَتْ له المعرفة ، وإنَّما يختلفون في القدرة على التعبير عمَّا في ضمائرهم وعدمِ ذلك ، وإنَّما لأَنَّهُمُ قلنا : إنَّ هذا أضعفُ مِنَ القولِ الذي حُكِيَ عن بعض الهنودِ ؛ اشترطوا في حصول المعرفة إزالة الشواغل ، وهذا لم يشترط شيئاً ، بل جعل المعرفة حاصلة لكلِّ مَنْ صَدَقَ عليه اسم الإيمانِ ، وأَنَّ مؤنةَ النظرِ لا يُحتاج إليها ! وهذا قول لاخفاء في بطلانِهِ ، وانعقاد الإجماع على خلافه ؛ إذْ معلوم قطعاً أنَّ عقائد الإيمانِ ليسَتْ كلُّها ضرورية ، بل منها ما يفتقرُ إلى دقيق النظرِ ، وكيف لا وقد اختلفت هذهِ الأُمَّةُ المشرفة وحدَها في العقائدِ اختلافاً كثيراً ، حتى إنَّها افترقَتْ على ثلاث وسبعينَ فِرقةً ، والمصيب منها فرقةٌ واحدةٌ ؟! ولهذا حكمَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بِأَنَّ جميعها في النار إلا واحدةً وأيضاً : فهذا القولُ يؤدي إلى أنَّ حَضَّهُ سبحانَهُ على النظر في آي مِنْ كتابه العزيز وأمرَهُ بذلك .. أمر بتحصيل الحاصل ! وكذا ما قَرَّرَهُ سبحانه في كتابه العزيزِ مِنْ أدلَّةِ العقائدِ ؛ كأدلة الوحدانية والبعث
The saying of one who said: 'There is no blind follower among the believers.' And weaker than this is the saying of some contemporaries: 'There is no blind follower among the believers, general and specific; rather, all of them have obtained knowledge, and they only differ in the ability to express what is in their consciences or not, and that is because they...' We said: This is weaker than the saying that was reported from some Indians, for they stipulated for the attainment of knowledge the removal of distractions, while this one stipulated nothing; rather he made knowledge obtained for everyone to whom the name of faith applies, and that the burden of reflection is not needed! And this is a saying whose falsity is not hidden, and there is consensus to the contrary, for it is known with certainty that the beliefs of faith are not all necessary, but some of them require precise reflection. How could it be otherwise when this honored community alone has differed greatly in matters of belief, to the extent that it split into seventy-three sects, and only one is correct. For this the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that all of them are in the Fire except one. Moreover, this saying leads to the conclusion that His urging, glorified, to reflect on the verses of His noble Book and His command to do so would be a command to obtain what is already obtained. Similarly, what He established in His noble Book of proofs for beliefs, like the proofs of oneness and resurrection.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that there is no blind imitation (taqlid) among believers and that every believer has certain knowledge. The author considers this even weaker than the previous Indian claim because at least the Indians required the removal of distractions, whereas this claim requires no effort at all, asserting knowledge is automatically possessed by anyone who claims faith. The author provides several arguments: (1) The beliefs of faith are not all self-evident; some require precise reflection. (2) The community itself has split into seventy-three sects, only one correctly guided, which shows that not all have certain knowledge. (3) The Prophet's hadith that all but one are in the Fire confirms this. (4) If knowledge were already present, then God's command to reflect on the Quran would be a command to obtain what is already obtained, which is absurd. (5) God provided proofs for beliefs like oneness and resurrection, which would be superfluous if knowledge were already present.

Correction: Sanusi argues that many beliefs require precise reflection (nazar) and that God's commands to reflect and the existence of proofs show that knowledge is not automatic.

Checkpoint

A) It makes God's command to reflect pointless.
B) It elevates the status of scholars.
C) It proves that all sects are correct.
D) It eliminates the need for prayer.

Key Takeaway
Faith does not automatically give certain knowledge; many beliefs require evidence and reflection, as shown by the need for proofs and the existence of differing sects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Prophet warned that only one sect will be saved. Have you ever critically examined whether your own beliefs are based on sound proofs or merely inherited tradition?
?
God commands us to reflect on His verses. Are you actively engaging in that reflection, or are you content with the level of certainty you have without seeking deeper understanding?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

Refuting the Claim of Universal Knowledge
Sanusi refutes the claim that no believer is a muqallid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multifaceted refutation Sanusi provides against the claim that all believers possess knowledge of faith without inquiry.

Core Idea
Faith requires inquiry; not all believers automatically know the creed correctly.

Sanusi confronts a dangerous claim: that every believer, regardless of knowledge or effort, already possesses perfect knowledge of the fundamentals of faith. This passage dismantles that claim using scripture, reason, and observable reality. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Read the opening lines to see the claim and its weaker variant. Understand what is being rejected.
The claim is that there is no muqallid among believers, meaning everyone has knowledge (ma'rifa) automatically.
2
First argument: consensus and the sects hadith
Sanusi points out that if knowledge were automatic, the umma would not have split into 73 sects. The Prophet's hadith indicates that only one sect is saved, proving that many lack correct knowledge.
3
Second argument: absurdity of commanding what is already obtained
If everyone already knew, then Allah's commands to reflect on the Quran would be pointless, and the proofs in the Quran would be redundant. This is rationally unacceptable.
4
Third argument: empirical evidence of widespread false beliefs
Sanusi appeals to observation: many common people hold heretical beliefs (corporealism, direction, denial of resurrection). Even some scholars fall into error, like the Tlemcen scholar who denied bodily resurrection.
This shows that knowledge is not automatic; study and inquiry are necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولُ مَنْ قالَ : لا مُقلد في المؤمنينَ . وأضعفُ مِنْ هذا : قولُ بعض المعاصرين : لا مُقلد المؤمنينَ عامهم وخاصهم ، وإنَّ جميعهم حصلَتْ له المعرفة ، وإنَّما يختلفون في القدرة على التعبير عمَّا في ضمائرهم وعدمِ ذلك ، وإنَّما لأَنَّهُمُ . قُلنا : إنَّ هذا أضعفُ مِنَ القولِ الذي حُكِيَ عن بعض الهنودِ ؛ اشترطوا في حصول المعرفة إزالة الشواغل ، وهذا لم يشترط شيئاً ، بل جعل المعرفة حاصلة لكلِّ مَنْ صَدَقَ عليه اسم الإيمانِ ، وأَنَّ مؤنةَ النظرِ لا يُحتاج إليها ! وهذا قول لاخفاء في بطلانِهِ ، وانعقاد الإجماع على خلافه ؛ إذْ معلوم قطعاً أنَّ عقائد الإيمانِ ليسَتْ كلُّها ضرورية ، بل منها ما يفتقرُ إلى دقيق النظرِ ، وكيف لا وقد اختلفت هذهِ الأُمَّةُ المشرفة وحدَها في العقائدِ اختلافاً كثيراً ، حتى إنَّها افترقَتْ على ثلاث وسبعينَ فِرقةً ، والمصيب منها فرقةٌ واحدةٌ ؟! ولهذا حكمَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بِأَنَّ جميعها في النار إلا واحدةً . وأيضاً : فهذا القولُ يؤدي إلى أنَّ حَضَّهُ سبحانَهُ على النظر في آي مِنْ كتابه العزيز وأمرَهُ بذلك .. أمر بتحصيل الحاصل ! وكذا ما قَرَّرَهُ سبحانه في كتابه العزيزِ مِنْ أدلَّةِ العقائدِ ؛ كأدلة الوحدانية والبعث والنبوة .. تقرير لما هو معلوم للكلِّ ! وهذا ممَّا يأباه كل عاقل . وأيضاً : فليس الخبرُ كالعِيانِ ، ونحنُ قد شاهدنا كثيراً ممَّنْ لم يأخذ في هذا العلم وله نجابةٌ في غيرِهِ مِنَ العلوم. . لا يحسنون العقائد تقليداً ، فضلاً أن يحسنوها بالنظرِ ! بل وشاهدنا كذلك بعضَ مَنْ أَخذَ في هذا العلم ولم يتقنه . أما العامَّةُ : فأكثرهم ممَّنْ لا يعتني بحضور مجالس العلماء ومخالطة أهل الخير ، نتحقَّقُ منهم اعتقاد التجسيم والجهة ، وتأثير الطبيعة ، وكون فعل الله تعالى لغرض ، وكون كلامه جلَّ وعلا حرفاً وصوتاً ، ومَرَّةً يتكلَّمُ ومَرَّةً يسكت كسائر البشر ، ونحوَ ذلكَ اعتقادات أهل الباطل ، وبعضُ اعتقاداتهم أجمع العلماء على كفْرِ معتقدها ، وبعضُها اختلفوا فيه . وكثيرٌ مِنْ أهل البادية ينكرُ البعثَ ، ولقد أخبرني بعضُ مَنْ أَثْقُ بهِ أنَّه سمع ذلك صريحاً منهم ، قال : وبعضُهم ممَّنْ يحفظ لفظ القرآن ، : ولقد حكى لي بعضُ أصحابنا مثلَ ذلكَ عمَّنْ لا يُظَنُّ به ذلكَ ممَّنْ يتعاطى العلمَ بتِلِمْسانَ ، وله أصل في رئاسة العلم ، قال : وصَرَّحَ لي بأنَّ رأيه وعقيدته ـ والعياذ بالله منهُ ومِنْ عقيدته - نفي المعادِ البدني ، كرأي الفلاسفة أبعدهم الله تعالى وأخلى منهمُ الأَرضَ ، قالَ : وجادلتُهُ في ذلكَ مِراراً ، فطبع على قلبه ولم يقبل ! وأظنُّ أنَّ المصيبة جاءَتِ الرجلَ مِنْ مطالعتِهِ بعض كتب الفلاسفة
The saying of whoever said: 'There is no muqallid (blind follower) among the believers.' And weaker than this is the saying of some contemporaries: 'There is no muqallid among the believers, both their common and their elite, and that all of them have obtained knowledge (ma'rifa), and they only differ in the ability to express what is in their hearts and the lack of that, and that is because they...' We said: 'Indeed this is weaker than the saying which was related from some Indians: they stipulated for obtaining knowledge the removal of distractions, but this one did not stipulate anything; rather he made knowledge obtained for everyone upon whom the name of faith applies, and that the burden of inquiry (nazar) is not needed! And this is a saying whose falseness is not hidden, and that consensus (ijma') has been reached contrary to it. For it is known with certainty that the beliefs (aqa'id) of faith are not all necessary (daruriyya), but rather some of them require precise inquiry. How could it not be, when this honored umma alone has differed in beliefs greatly, to the extent that it split into seventy-three sects, and the correct one among them is only one sect? And for this the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that all of them are in the Fire except one. And also: This saying leads to the point that His urgings (subhanahu) upon inquiry (nazar) in the verses of His Mighty Book and His commanding that is a command to obtain what is already obtained! And likewise what He (subhanahu) established in His Mighty Book of proofs of the beliefs, such as the proofs of Oneness, the Resurrection, and Prophethood, are affirmations of what is known to everyone! And this is something that every rational person rejects. And also: Report (khabar) is not like direct observation (iyan). And we have seen many of those who did not engage in this science (ilm) and have intelligence in other sciences, they do not perfect the beliefs by blind following, let alone perfecting them by inquiry! Rather we have also seen some of those who engaged in this science and did not master it. As for the common people (amma), most of them are among those who do not attend to being present in the gatherings of scholars and mixing with the people of goodness, we ascertain from them the belief in corporealism (tajsim) and direction (jiha), the influence of nature, that the action of Allah (ta'ala) is for a purpose, that His speech (kalam) (jalla wa 'ala) is letter and sound, and that sometimes He speaks and sometimes He is silent like other human beings, and similar beliefs of the people of falsehood. Some of their beliefs the scholars have unanimously agreed upon the disbelief (kufr) of the one who holds them, and some of them they differed about. And many of the Bedouins deny the Resurrection. And some of those whom I trust informed me that he heard that explicitly from them. He said: And some of them are among those who memorize the wording of the Quran. And some of our companions related to me the like of that from one who would not be suspected of that, among those who practice knowledge in Tlemcen, and he has a foundation in the leadership of knowledge. He said: And he declared to me that his opinion and belief – and refuge is sought with Allah from him and from his belief – is the denial of the bodily resurrection, like the opinion of the philosophers, may Allah remove them far and clear the earth of them. He said: And I argued with him in that repeatedly, but his heart was sealed and he did not accept! And I think that the affliction came to the man from his reading some books of the philosophers.'
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that there is no muqallid (blind follower) among believers, i.e., that all believers possess knowledge (ma'rifa) of the fundamentals of faith without the need for inquiry (nazar). The author begins by stating that the weakest form of this claim is the saying of some contemporaries who assert that both the common and elite among believers all have knowledge, differing only in their ability to express it. The author then argues that this is even weaker than the position of some Indians who at least stipulated the removal of distractions for knowledge, whereas this claim requires no condition at all. The author declares this saying to be obviously false and contrary to consensus (ijma'), since it is certain that not all beliefs of faith are necessary (daruriyya); some require precise inquiry. The evidence for this is the well-known splitting of the Muslim umma into seventy-three sects, with only one being saved, as per the Prophet's hadith. Furthermore, this claim implies that Allah's command to reflect on the Quranic verses is a command to obtain what is already obtained, which is absurd. The author also points out that the proofs of oneness, resurrection, and prophethood in the Quran would then be affirmations of what is already known to everyone, which every rational person rejects. The author then appeals to empirical observation: we see many intelligent people who have not studied this science (kalam) fail to perfect the beliefs even by blind following, let alone by inquiry. Even some who have studied it do not master it. As for the common people, they often hold heretical beliefs such as corporealism (tajsim), direction (jiha), influence of nature, purpose in divine actions, and that God's speech is letters and sound, sometimes speaking sometimes silent like humans. Some of these beliefs are unanimously considered kufr, others are disputed. The author then provides a concrete example: many Bedouins deny the bodily resurrection. He recounts a trusted informant who heard that explicitly from them. Then an even more striking case: a scholar in Tlemcen, known for his knowledge, who openly denied the bodily resurrection, adopting the opinion of the philosophers. Despite repeated argumentation, his heart was sealed. The author attributes this to his reading of philosophical books. This passage thus serves to demonstrate, through scriptural, rational, and empirical arguments, that the claim of universal necessary knowledge is false and dangerous.

Key Terms
taqlid
muqallid
ma'rifa
nazar
daruriyya
ijma'
tajsim
jiha
kalam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that simply being a Muslim automatically grants full and correct knowledge of all creedal matters without study or inquiry.
Correction: Sanusi shows that many believers, including common people and even some scholars, hold heretical beliefs, proving that knowledge is not automatic. Faith requires inquiry and learning.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, which of the following is a consequence of the claim that no believer is a muqallid?
A) It would make Allah's command to reflect on the Quran pointless.
B) It would mean that the Prophet's hadith about 73 sects is false.
C) It would require that all believers are scholars of kalam.
D) It would contradict the consensus of the umma.

Key Takeaway
The claim of universal automatic knowledge is refuted by consensus, rational necessity, and observable reality; correct belief requires diligent inquiry and learning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that because you believe in Allah and the basics of Islam, your aqeedah is automatically correct and needs no further study? In light of this lesson, what specific 'heretical' belief might you unknowingly hold that you need to examine today? Commit to investigating it with a reliable scholar this week.
?
Sanusi mentions a scholar in Tlemcen who denied bodily resurrection after reading philosophy. What intellectual influences—books, websites, social media—are you exposed to that could be subtly undermining your aqeedah? List one and decide how to protect yourself from it starting now.
?
Most of the common people Sanusi describes never attend scholars' gatherings. Where do you get your understanding of faith? If you rely on your own reading or casual sources, are you confident you have not fallen into error in any of the beliefs Sanusi lists (e.g., direction, Allah's speech)? What concrete step will you take this week to verify your own creed?

The Ruling on Uttering Shahada Without Understanding
Sanusi presents the scholars' ruling on one who says shahada without understanding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling of scholars concerning a person who pronounces the shahada but does not understand its meaning or distinguish the messenger from the one sent.

Core Idea
Uttering the shahada without understanding has no value in Islam.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a critical issue: can a person be considered Muslim simply by pronouncing the shahada without any understanding? He cites the ruling of the scholars of Bijaya and other investigators, which may seem harsh but underscores the importance of knowledge in faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the ruling carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the condition mentioned: the person does not distinguish between the messenger and the one sent.
The passage specifically mentions muqallids (blind followers).
2
Identify the key condition
The ruling applies to someone who says the shahada but does not know its meaning or does not distinguish the messenger from Allah. Consider why this distinction is critical.
The shahada declares belief in Allah and His messenger; mixing them up is serious.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: What does it mean to have 'no share in Islam'? Does it mean they are not Muslims at all, or that their Islam is deficient? How does this relate to the importance of learning?
The scholars' ruling emphasizes that faith requires understanding, not just words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ ينطق بكلمتي الشهادةِ ولا يُميّزُ بينَ الرسول والمرسل وبعضُ المُقلدين ينطق بكلمتي الشهادةِ مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يعرف معناها ، ولا أن يُميّر الرسولَ مِنَ المرسل ، وفي مثلِهِ وقعَتْ أجوبة علماء بجاية وغيرهم من المحققين : أنَّ مثل هذا لا يُضَرَبُ له في الإسلام بنصيب . فضل العلماء على العامة والعاقل في الحقيقةِ مَنْ أنصفَ مِنْ نفسِهِ ، فوالله ؛ لولا فضله تعالى وتوفيقه لمخالطة العلم وأهلِهِ .. لَمَا كُنَّا نُحسِنُ عقائدَ الإِيمَانِ بِمُجرَّدِ التقليد فضلاً عن النظرِ ، ولكنَّا في أوديةٍ مِن اعتقاداتِ أهلِ الباطل نهيمُ ، وعجباً لعاقل يجهلُ الضروريَّاتِ ! حتى لم يشعر بحال نفسِهِ قبل مخالطة العلمِ ، ولا شعرَ بحالِ العوام ومَنْ أعرض عن النظرِ جملةً ولقد ألَّفَ علماء السنَّةِ رضي الله عنهم تواليف مختصرةً
Whoever pronounces the two words of the shahada but does not distinguish between the messenger and the one sent? And some muqallids pronounce the two words of the shahada without knowing their meaning, nor do they distinguish the messenger from the one sent. Regarding such a person, the scholars of Bijaya and other investigators have given rulings that such a one has no share in Islam. The virtue of scholars over the common people. The truly intelligent person is one who is fair to himself. For by Allah, were it not for His grace and facilitation through mixing with learning and its people, we would not be able to properly hold the beliefs of faith even by taqlīd, let alone by rational inquiry! Rather, we would be wandering in the valleys of the beliefs of the people of falsehood. And it is amazing that a person of intelligence is ignorant of the necessary matters! So that he does not even perceive the state of his own soul before mixing with learning, nor does he perceive the state of the common people and those who turn away from rational inquiry entirely. Indeed, the scholars of the Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them, have composed concise treatises.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage discusses two related issues. First, the author addresses those who pronounce the shahada but do not understand its meaning or do not distinguish the messenger from the one who sent him. The scholars of Bijaya and others have ruled that such a person has no share in Islam. Second, the author extols the virtue of scholars over the common people. He explains that without Allah's grace and the opportunity to mix with scholars, we would not be able to correctly hold the beliefs of faith even by taqlīd, let alone by reasoned inquiry. Indeed, without this, we would be wandering in false beliefs. He finds it amazing that an intelligent person can be ignorant of the necessary matters of faith and not realize his own state before learning. The author concludes by noting that Sunni scholars have composed concise works on this topic.

Correction: The scholars ruled that such a person has no share in Islam, indicating that understanding is essential.

Uttering the shahada without understanding its meaning and without distinguishing the messenger from Allah renders one's Islam deficient according to the scholars.

The Virtue of Scholars and the Danger of Ignorance
Sanusi extols scholars and warns against ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the immense virtue of scholars and the necessity of learning for correct faith, exceeding even blind imitation.

Core Idea
Without scholars, we would be lost in false beliefs.

After emphasizing the importance of understanding, Sanusi turns to praise scholars and highlight the grace of Allah in enabling us to learn. He expresses amazement at intelligent people who remain ignorant of necessary religious matters and notes that even taqlid (imitation) is insufficient without proper learning.

1

2
Understand the role of divine grace
The author thanks Allah for enabling him to mix with scholars. Without this grace, even taqlid would not lead to correct beliefs.
He mentions that without learning, they would wander in falsehood.
3
Reflect on the danger of ignorance
The author is amazed that intelligent people can be ignorant of necessary matters (الضروريات). Consider how this applies to those who avoid learning.

The Muqallid Who Cannot Distinguish Messenger from Mursal
Sanusi discusses the ruling on those who pronounce the shahada without understanding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the validity of the shahada requires at least minimal understanding of its meaning and the distinction between the messenger and the sender.

Core Idea
Mere utterance of the shahada without understanding does not make one a Muslim.

The shahada is the door to Islam, but it is not a mere formula. The scholars of Bijaya addressed a critical question: what about someone who recites the shahada without knowing what it means? In this passage, Sanusi presents their ruling, which underscores the necessity of basic comprehension for faith to be valid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once, then its literal translation. Let the wording settle before analyzing.
Notice the term 'muqallid' — a blind follower who does not understand.
2
Understand the scenario
The passage describes a person who pronounces the shahada but lacks knowledge of its meaning and cannot distinguish the messenger (Prophet Muhammad) from the one who sent him (Allah).
The inability to distinguish indicates profound ignorance.
3
Reflect on the ruling
The scholars of Bijaya ruled that such a person has no share in Islam. This means their declaration is invalid because it lacks the necessary understanding.
This emphasizes the importance of knowledge (ma'rifa) in faith.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
Some think that simply uttering the words is enough. This passage corrects that: faith requires at least minimal comprehension.
This is a key principle in kalam and fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ مَنْ ينطق بكلمتي الشهادةِ ولا يُميّزُ بينَ الرسول والمرسل ] وبعضُ المُقلدين ينطق بكلمتي الشهادةِ مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يعرف معناها ، ولا أن يُميّر الرسولَ مِنَ المرسل ، وفي مثلِهِ وقعَتْ أجوبة علماء بجاية وغيرهم من المحققين : أنَّ مثل هذا لا يُضَرَبُ له في الإسلام بنصيب .
[He who pronounces the two words of shahada and does not distinguish between the messenger and the one sent] And some of the muqallidun (blind followers) pronounce the two words of shahada without knowing their meaning, nor do they distinguish the messenger from the one sent. Regarding such a person, the answers of the scholars of Bijaya and other investigators occurred: that such a person is not granted a share in Islam.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling concerning the muqallid (blind follower) who utters the testimony of faith (shahada) but does not understand its meaning or distinguish between the messenger (al-rasul) and the one sent (al-mursal). The author first states the situation: some muqallidun recite the shahada without comprehension of its implications; they cannot even differentiate the Prophet from Allah who sent him? The phrase likely means they do not know what the shahada entails regarding the messengerhood of Muhammad. Then he mentions that the scholars of Bijaya (a city in Algeria) and other researchers gave a judgment: such a person is not granted a share in Islam, meaning his Islam is invalid because he lacks the basic knowledge required. This emphasizes the necessity of at least minimal understanding of the shahada for the validity of one's faith.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The scholars of Bijaya ruled that such a person is not granted a share in Islam, showing that minimal understanding is required for faith to be valid.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a person who pronounces the shahada but cannot distinguish between the messenger and the one sent?
A) He is still a Muslim because he uttered the words.
B) He is not granted a share in Islam according to the scholars of Bijaya.
C) He is considered a hypocrite.
D) He must repeat the shahada with proper knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Faith requires at least minimal understanding of the meaning of the shahada and who the messenger is.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Every Believer is a Knower of Allah: Al-Baqillani's Principle
Al-Baqillani's statement on knowledge of Allah in every believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Baqillani's assertion that every true believer possesses certain knowledge of Allah, and why some believers cannot articulate that knowledge.

Core Idea
Every true believer has direct knowledge of Allah, even if they cannot express it.

This lesson presents a key statement from the renowned scholar al-Baqillani, addressing a common question about faith and knowledge. The passage clarifies that all believers have ma'rifa (knowledge) of Allah, but their ability to articulate it varies. Understanding this distinction helps resolve apparent contradictions between simple faith and scholarly theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation to grasp the basic claim and the objector's question.
2
Identify the two categories of believers
Notice that al-Baqillani divides believers into two groups: those who can express and prove their faith, and those who have certainty but cannot articulate it.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters for understanding faith—every believer has genuine knowledge, so lack of eloquence does not indicate lack of faith.
This is a key point in Sunni creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قد نُقِلَ عن القاضي أبي بكر بن الطيب رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ أَنَّهُ قالَ : لا يُوجَدُ مؤمن إلا وهو عارف بالله تعالى ، إلا أنَّ أحوالهم في ذلكَ ؛ فمنهم قوي القريحة على أنْ يُعبّرَ على ما في قلبه ويبرهن عليه ، ومنهم مَنْ عرفَ الله يقيناً ولا قدرة لهُ أنْ يُعبّرَ على ما في قلبه .
If you say: It has been transmitted from al-Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: 'There does not exist a believer except that he is a knower of Allah, the Exalted, except that their states regarding that differ; some of them are strong in intellect to express what is in his heart and to prove it, and some of them know Allah with certainty but have no ability to express what is in his heart.'
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer format. The objector quotes al-Qadi al-Baqillani's statement that every believer is necessarily a knower (arif) of Allah, meaning that true faith inherently includes certain knowledge. The answer explains that believers indeed all have this knowledge, but their states differ: some are intellectually strong and can articulate and provide proofs for what is in their hearts, while others know Allah with certainty but lack the ability to express or demonstrate it. This maintains that even the simplest believer has genuine ma'rifa, but not all can explain it. This addresses the concern that some believers may appear ignorant yet still possess true faith.

مؤمن
قريحة
يقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only scholars have true knowledge of Allah.
Correction: Al-Baqillani asserts that every believer has knowledge of Allah, though their ability to express it varies.

Checkpoint

A) He is not a true believer.
B) He still knows Allah with certainty but lacks the ability to express it.
C) He must learn from scholars before his faith is valid.
D) He is excused because he is a muqallid.

Key Takeaway
Every true believer possesses certain knowledge of Allah, but not all can articulate or prove it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Is your faith grounded in yaqin (certainty) or mere imitation? According to this lesson, every true believer possesses direct knowledge. If you feel uncertain, what is missing, and what step will you take today to seek that certainty?

Resolving the Apparent Contradiction in al-Baqillani's Statement
Sanusi refutes the objection that al-Baqillani's claim contradicts the necessity of proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi resolves the apparent contradiction between al-Baqillani's claim that every believer is a knower of God and the necessity of rational proofs for faith.

Core Idea
True faith requires inner knowledge, not just outward imitation.

Sanusi addresses a crucial objection: if al-Baqillani says every believer is a knower of God, does that mean proofs are unnecessary? The objector cites reports that knowledge of God is innate and that some believers cannot articulate proofs. Sanusi responds by distinguishing between God's judgment and our judgment, and between true knowledge and mere imitation. This lesson walks through his careful reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection that al-Baqillani's statement seems to contradict the need for proofs. Notice the reports about innate knowledge and inability to express proofs.
The objector thinks this is exactly what Sanusi denied earlier.
2
Identify Sanusi's response
Sanusi says 'it is not exactly it, nor does it indicate it.' He then distinguishes between two judgments: God's judgment (based on reality) and our judgment (based on appearances).
3
Grasp the concept of 'qasr ifrad'
Understand that al-Baqillani's restriction (qasr) means only true knowers are believers in God's sight. This refutes those who think a non-knower could be a believer.
Qasr ifrad restricts the attribute to the subject exclusively.
4
Relate to faith and knowledge
Connect this to al-Baqillani's principle that true faith (iman) is assent dependent on knowledge, not on imitation, conjecture, doubt, or illusion.
This clarifies that the statement does not negate the need for proofs; it defines the inner reality of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله القاضي الباقلاني : لا يوجد مؤمن إلا وهو عارف بالله تعالى فإن قلت : قد نُقِلَ عن القاضي أبي بكر بن الطيب رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ أَنَّهُ قالَ : لا يُوجَدُ مؤمن إلا وهو عارف بالله تعالى ، إلا أنَّ أحوالهم في ذلكَ ؛ فمنهم قوي القريحة على أنْ يُعبّرَ على ما في قلبه ويبرهن عليه ، ومنهم مَنْ عرفَ الله يقيناً ولا قدرة لهُ أنْ يُعبّرَ على ما في قلبه ، ونُقِلَ عن طائفة مِنْ أهل العلم أنَّ الله معروف بضرورة العقل، وأنَّهُ غرزَ معرفةَ وجودِهِ في خلقِهِ ، وما أُقيمَ مِنَ الأَدلَّةِ على ذلكَ إِنَّما استدلال على أنواع الضرورة ، وظاهر هذا عين ما أنكرتَ ! قلتُ : ليس عينه ، ولا يدلُّ عليه . أما قولُ القاضي : فهو جارٍ على أصلِهِ وأصل الجمهورِ مِنْ أَنَّ التقليد لا تحصلُ معَهُ حقيقة الإيمانِ ، وإنَّما تحصل مع المعرفة ، ولهذا كانت حقيقة الإيمانِ عندَ القاضي هو التصديق التابع للمعرفة ، واحترز بقوله : ( التابع للمعرفةِ ) مِنَ التصديق التابع للاعتقادِ التقليدي أو التابع للظنّ أو الشكّ أو الوهم ، فمعنى قوله : ( لا يُوجَدُ مؤمن إلا وهو عارف باللهِ تعالى ) لا يُوجَدُ مؤمن شرعاً ـ أي : في حكم الله تعالى المبني على التحقيقِ وما في نفس الأمر ، لا في حكمنا نحنُ المبني على الظواهر - إلا وهو عارفُ ؛ أي : فمَنْ ليس بعارف ؛ كالمقلد ونحوه .. فليس بمؤمن عندَ اللهِ سبحانه فالقصر في لفظه قصرُ إفراد ؛ ردّاً على مَنْ يتوهَّمُ اشتراك العارفِ
The statement of Qadi al-Baqillani: 'There is no believer except that he is a knower of Allah, Exalted is He.' For if you say: It has been transmitted from Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: 'There is no believer except that he is a knower of Allah, Exalted is He. However, their states in that are different: among them are those strong of intellect such that they can express what is in their hearts and offer proof, and among them are those who know Allah with certainty but have no ability to express what is in their hearts.' And it has been transmitted from a group of scholars that Allah is known by necessity of reason, and that He implanted knowledge of His existence in His creation, and that the proofs established for that are only demonstrations of types of necessity. The apparent meaning of this is exactly what you denied! I say: It is not exactly it, nor does it indicate it. As for the statement of the Qadi, it proceeds according to his principle and the principle of the majority, that imitation (taqlid) does not yield the reality of faith; rather, it only yields knowledge. Hence, the reality of faith according to the Qadi is assent (tasdiq) dependent on knowledge. By his saying 'dependent on knowledge' he excluded assent dependent on imitative belief or dependent on conjecture, doubt, or illusion. So the meaning of his saying 'there is no believer except that he is a knower of Allah, Exalted is He' is: there is no believer in the religious sense — i.e., in the judgment of Allah, Exalted is He, based on verification and the real state of affairs, not in our judgment based on outward appearances — except that he is a knower. That is, whoever is not a knower, like the imitator and the like, is not a believer in the sight of Allah, Exalted is He. Thus the restriction in his statement is a restriction of exclusivity (qasr ifrad), as a refutation of those who imagine the sharing of the knower...
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. Sanusi presents an objection based on reports from al-Baqillani and others that seem to claim that all believers are knowers of God and that knowledge of God is innate, which might contradict the earlier emphasis on the need for proofs. The objector says this appears to be exactly what Sanusi denied (i.e., that faith can occur without inquiry). Sanusi responds by distinguishing between outward judgment (our judgment based on appearances) and God's judgment (based on the real state of affairs). He explains that al-Baqillani's statement is based on his principle that true faith (haqiqat al-iman) is assent (tasdiq) that is dependent on knowledge (ma'rifa), not on mere imitation, conjecture, doubt, or illusion. So by saying 'no believer except that he is a knower,' he means that in God's judgment, no one is a believer unless they have genuine knowledge; the imitator is not a true believer in God's sight, even though we may judge him as a believer outwardly. The phrase 'qasr ifrad' indicates a restrictive limitation, meaning that the attribute of 'being a knower' is confined to the believer, refuting those who think a non-knower could share in the title. This resolves the apparent contradiction: the judge is speaking about the inner reality of faith, not the outward judgment.

Key Terms
عارف
مؤمن
تقليد
تصديق
معرفة
قصر إفراد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Baqillani's statement that every believer is a knower of God means that rational proofs are unnecessary and that faith is purely innate.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that al-Baqillani is referring to God's judgment of the inner reality of faith, which requires genuine knowledge (not mere imitation). This does not negate the need for proofs; rather, it defines true faith as knowledge-based assent.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's explanation, what does al-Baqillani mean by saying 'there is no believer except that he is a knower of Allah'?
A) Every person who calls themselves a Muslim is automatically a knower of God
B) Only those who have explicit proofs are believers
C) In God's judgment, a true believer must have genuine knowledge, not mere imitation
D) Faith is possible without any knowledge

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqillani's statement means that in God's judgment, true believers possess inner knowledge, not mere imitation; this does not negate the need for proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God judges your faith based on inner knowledge, not outward actions or imitation, do you actually know Him—or have you merely adopted the beliefs of those around you? What would change in your life if you truly sought ma'rifa starting today?
?
You may call yourself a believer, but are you willing to stand before Allah and claim that your faith is based on certainty, not on comfort or conformity? What step can you take this week to move from taqlid to tahqiq?
?
Think of a moment when you could not defend your faith but still felt sure of it. Does that confidence come from knowledge of Allah, or from habit? How can you strengthen that certainty so it becomes unshakable even when you cannot articulate it?
