⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذهب الثاني : أنَّ العذابَ إنَّما يحسنُ في حق الكافر دونَ المسلم ، وهو مذهب المرجئة ، وجزموا بنفي عقابِ مَنْ مَاتَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الكبائر قبل أن يُوفَّق للتوبة
واحتجوا بقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ الْخِزْيَ الْيَوْمَ وَالسُّوءَ عَلَى الْكَفِرِينَ [النحل : ۲۷] ، ودخولُ النارِ خزي ؛ بدليل : ﴿ مَن تُدْخِلِ النَّارَ فَقَدْ أَخْزَيْنَتَهُ ﴾ [آل عمران : ۱۹۲] ، فهو خاص إذاً بالكافرين .
وبقوله تعالى : قَدْ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْنَا أَنَّ الْعَذَابَ عَلَى مَن كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى [طه : ٤٨] ، والألفُ واللام في ( العذابِ ) : للعموم . وبقولِهِ تعالى : ( كُلَّمَا أُلْقِيَ فِيهَا فوج ...) [الملك : ٨) الآية .
وبقوله تعالى : لَا يَصْلَنَهَا إِلَّا الْأَشْقَى * الَّذِي كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى [الليل : ١٥ - ١٦ ] . وبقولِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ : ﴿ وَهَلْ تُجرِى إِلَّا الْكَفُور ) [سبا : ۱۷] ، والكَفُورُ : لفظ مبالغة ، فوجبَ أنْ يختص بالكافِرِ
و لا يُقالُ : يعارضُهُ قولُهُ تعالى : مَن يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا يُجْزَ بِهِ ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲۳) لأنَّا نقول (١) : يُرجحُ عندَ التعارض أي الوعد على آي الوعيد ؛ لأنَّ رحمته تعالى وفضلَهُ أغلب
وبقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ و يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوهٌ . . . [آل عمران : ١٠٦] الآية .
وبقوله جلَّ وعزَّ : ﴿ وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَيذٍ تُسفِرَةٌ ﴾ [عبس: ٣٨] الآيةَ .
وبقوله تعالى : ﴿ يَعِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ لَا تَقْنَطُوا مِن رَّحْمَةِ الله ... [الزمر : ٥٣] الآيةَ ، والمراد : المؤمنون ؛ لأنَّ الإضافة تشعر بتشريف ما ، ولا شرفَ للكافر .
والجواب عن الجميع : أنَّ الآياتِ المخصصة العذابَ بالكافر مرادُها عذابٌ وخزي خاص ، وهو الذي يقتضي الخلود ، ولا فلاح بعدَهُ والعياذُ باللهِ ، ولا خفاءَ أَنَّ ذلك خاص بالكافِرِ
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ يَعِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ * فهو عام يقبلُ التخصيص، وأيضاً : فيحتملُ أنَّ المراد حضُّ العصاة على التوبة والرجوع إلى الله تعالى ، وألا يقنطوا بمواقعة الذنبِ مِنْ رحمة الله تعالى حتى يصدَّهم ذلك عن التوبة ، ويدلُّ عليه قوله تعالى إثْرَ هذهِ الآية : ﴿ وَأَنبُوا إِلَى رَبِّكُمْ وَأَسْلِمُوا لَهُ ... [الزمر : ٥٤] الآيةَ
The second doctrine: that punishment is only fitting for the disbeliever, not the Muslim. This is the doctrine of the Murji'ah, and they affirm the negation of punishment for one who dies among the people of major sins before being granted repentance.
They argued with His saying, the Exalted: 'Indeed, disgrace today and evil are upon the disbelievers' [al-Nahl 16:27]. Entering the Fire is disgrace, as evidenced by: 'Whoever You admit to the Fire, You have disgraced him' [Aal 'Imran 3:192]. So it is specific to disbelievers.
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'It has been revealed to us that the punishment is upon whoever denies and turns away' [Ta-Ha 20:48]. The definite article in 'al-'adhab' indicates generality. And with His saying, the Exalted: 'Whenever a group is thrown into it...' [al-Mulk 67:8].
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'None shall enter it except the most wretched, who denied and turned away' [al-Layl 92:15-16]. And with His saying, the Majestic and High: 'And do We requite except the ungrateful?' [Saba' 34:17]. 'Al-kafur' is an intensive form, so it must be specific to the disbeliever.
And it cannot be said that it is contradicted by His saying, the Exalted: 'Whoever does evil shall be recompensed for it' [al-Nisa' 4:123]. Because we say: when there is contradiction, one gives precedence to the promise over the verses of threat, for His mercy and grace are predominant.
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'On the Day when faces become white and faces become black...' [Aal 'Imran 3:106].
And with His saying, the Majestic and High: 'Some faces that Day will be bright' ['Abasa 80:38].
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of God...' [al-Zumar 39:53]. The intended are the believers, because the possessive pronoun indicates some honor, and the disbeliever has no honor.
And the answer to all of this: the verses that specify punishment for the disbeliever are intended to mean a specific punishment and disgrace, which necessitates eternity, and there is no success after it—God forbid—and it is clear that that is specific to the disbeliever.
As for His saying, the Exalted: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves' it is general and admits specification. Also, it is possible that the intended meaning is to urge the sinners to repentance and return to God, and not to despair of God's mercy due to committing sin so that it would prevent them from repentance. This is indicated by His saying, the Exalted, after this verse: 'And turn to your Lord and submit to Him...' [al-Zumar 39:54].
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Murji'ah doctrine on punishment. First, it states the doctrine: punishment is only fitting for disbelievers, not Muslims, and those who die with major sins without repentance will not be punished. Then it lists their proofs from the Quran: verses that mention disgrace and punishment specifically for disbelievers (16:27, 3:192, 20:48, 67:8, 92:15-16, 34:17), a verse that might seem to threaten all (4:123) but they claim it is outweighed by mercy, and verses that seem to promise mercy to believers (3:106, 80:38, 39:53). The author then provides the answer: the verses specifying punishment for disbelievers refer to eternal punishment, which is indeed specific to them, while verses like 39:53 are general and can be specified to urge repentance, as indicated by the following verse (39:54). The passage thus defends the Sunni position that Muslim sinners may be punished temporarily but not eternally.

Key Terms
المرجئة
العذاب
الكبائر
الخزي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Murji'ah, who is subject to punishment?
A) All sinners
B) Only disbelievers
C) Only those who die without repentance
D) Both Muslims and disbelievers

Key Takeaway
The Murji'ah believe punishment is exclusive to disbelievers, citing verses on disgrace as proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you sometimes assume that because you are a Muslim, Allah will not punish you? How does the Murji'ah doctrine expose this dangerous assumption?
?
Have you ever selectively used a Quranic verse to justify leniency toward your sins, like the Murji'ah use 16:27? What would it take for you to repent sincerely today?
?
If you truly believed that your sins have no consequence in the Hereafter, how would that change your attitude toward repentance? Are you willing to examine whether you hold any Murji'ah-like thinking in your heart?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
12 min
Further Proofs of the Murji'ah
The author lists additional Quranic proofs of the Murji'ah, including verses on punishment and mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be familiar with the additional Quranic proofs used by the Murji'ah to support their doctrine on punishment.

Core Idea
The Murji'ah amass Quranic verses to argue that punishment is only for those who deny and turn away.

The Murji'ah do not rely on just one proof; they bring several verses that appear to limit punishment to disbelievers and those who reject faith. In this lesson, we go through their key scriptural arguments. This will set the stage for the refutation in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
List the verses cited
Notice the sequence of verses: 20:48, 67:8, 92:15-16, 34:17, 4:123, 3:106, 80:38, 39:53. Each is used to show punishment is for disbelievers or mercy is for believers.
2
Understand their reasoning
For each verse, they interpret words like 'al-'adhab' (punishment) as general, or 'al-kafur' (ungrateful) as intensive form specific to disbelievers. They also argue that when verses contradict, mercy verses should be given precedence.
Their handling of verse 4:123 is interesting: they acknowledge it seems to threaten all, but they prioritize mercy.
3
Analyze the mercy verses
The last verses (3:106, 80:38, 39:53) are used to show that believers will be honored and spared punishment. They interpret the possessive 'My servants' as indicating honor specific to believers.

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Murji'ah doctrine on punishment. First, it states the doctrine: punishment is only fitting for disbelievers, not Muslims, and those who die with major sins without repentance will not be punished. How do the Murji'ah handle the apparent contradiction from verse 4:123?
A) They consider it abrogated

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses like 'Do not despair of the mercy of God,' do you apply them to yourself as a believer or use them to excuse ongoing sin? Which of your current habits are you justifying with Allah's mercy rather than repenting from?
?
The Murji'ah argued that punishment is only for those who deny and turn away. Is there a sin you commit while knowing it is wrong but telling yourself 'I still have faith, so I won't be punished'? What would it take for you to truly fear the verses of threat?
?
You saw how the Murji'ah prioritized verses of promise over verses of threat. When you read the Quran, do you selectively focus on verses that comfort you and ignore those that demand change? What is one verse of threat that you have been avoiding applying to your life?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
10 min
Refutation of the Murji'ah Proofs
The author refutes the Murji'ah proofs by distinguishing eternal punishment for disbelievers from temporary punishment for Muslim sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni scholars refute the Murji'ah proofs by distinguishing between eternal and temporary punishment.

Core Idea
The verses cited by the Murji'ah refer to eternal punishment, while mercy verses encourage repentance.

Now we come to the Sunni response to the Murji'ah arguments. The key is that the punishment verses are about eternal, never-ending punishment, which is indeed only for disbelievers. The mercy verses, on the other hand, are general and aimed at calling sinners to repentance. This refutation preserves both divine justice and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer
The author states that the verses specifying punishment for disbelievers refer to a specific punishment that necessitates eternity. That is indeed for disbelievers only.
2
Examine the handling of the mercy verse
For verse 39:53, the author says it is general and can be specified. The intended meaning is to encourage sinners to repent, not to guarantee forgiveness without repentance.
The following verse (39:54) shows it is about turning to Allah.
3
Reflect on the overall refutation
This answer reconciles all the verses: the threat verses apply to eternal punishment for disbelievers, while the mercy verses apply to the possibility of forgiveness through repentance for believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذهب الثاني : أنَّ العذابَ إنَّما يحسنُ في حق الكافر دونَ المسلم ، وهو مذهب المرجئة ، وجزموا بنفي عقابِ مَنْ مَاتَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الكبائر قبل أن يُوفَّق للتوبة

وبقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ و يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوهٌ . . . [آل عمران : ١٠٦] الآية .
وبقوله جلَّ وعزَّ : ﴿ وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَيذٍ تُسفِرَةٌ ﴾ [عبس: ٣٨] الآيةَ .
وبقوله تعالى : ﴿ يَعِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ لَا تَقْنَطُوا مِن رَّحْمَةِ الله ... [الزمر : ٥٣] الآيةَ ، والمراد : المؤمنون ؛ لأنَّ الإضافة تشعر بتشريف ما ، ولا شرفَ للكافر .
والجواب عن الجميع : أنَّ الآياتِ المخصصة العذابَ بالكافر مرادُها عذابٌ وخزي خاص ، وهو الذي يقتضي الخلود ، ولا فلاح بعدَهُ والعياذُ باللهِ ، ولا خفاءَ أَنَّ ذلك خاص بالكافِرِ
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ يَعِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ * فهو عام يقبلُ التخصيص، وأيضاً : فيحتملُ أنَّ المراد حضُّ العصاة على التوبة والرجوع إلى الله تعالى ، وألا يقنطوا بمواقعة الذنبِ مِنْ رحمة الله تعالى حتى يصدَّهم ذلك عن التوبة ، ويدلُّ عليه قوله تعالى إثْرَ هذهِ الآية : ﴿ وَأَنبُوا إِلَى رَبِّكُمْ وَأَسْلِمُوا لَهُ ... [الزمر : ٥٤] الآيةَ
The second doctrine: that punishment is only fitting for the disbeliever, not the Muslim. This is the doctrine of the Murji'ah, and they affirm the negation of punishment for one who dies among the people of major sins before being granted repentance.
They argued with His saying, the Exalted: 'Indeed, disgrace today and evil are upon the disbelievers' [al-Nahl 16:27]. Entering the Fire is disgrace, as evidenced by: 'Whoever You admit to the Fire, You have disgraced him' [Aal 'Imran 3:192]. So it is specific to disbelievers.
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'It has been revealed to us that the punishment is upon whoever denies and turns away' [Ta-Ha 20:48]. The definite article in 'al-'adhab' indicates generality. And with His saying, the Exalted: 'Whenever a group is thrown into it...' [al-Mulk 67:8].
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'None shall enter it except the most wretched, who denied and turned away' [al-Layl 92:15-16]. And with His saying, the Majestic and High: 'And do We requite except the ungrateful?' [Saba' 34:17]. 'Al-kafur' is an intensive form, so it must be specific to the disbeliever.
And it cannot be said that it is contradicted by His saying, the Exalted: 'Whoever does evil shall be recompensed for it' [al-Nisa' 4:123]. Because we say: when there is contradiction, one gives precedence to the promise over the verses of threat, for His mercy and grace are predominant.
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'On the Day when faces become white and faces become black...' [Aal 'Imran 3:106].
And with His saying, the Majestic and High: 'Some faces that Day will be bright' ['Abasa 80:38].
And with His saying, the Exalted: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of God...' [al-Zumar 39:53]. The intended are the believers, because the possessive pronoun indicates some honor, and the disbeliever has no honor.
And the answer to all of this: the verses that specify punishment for the disbeliever are intended to mean a specific punishment and disgrace, which necessitates eternity, and there is no success after it—God forbid—and it is clear that that is specific to the disbeliever.
As for His saying, the Exalted: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves' it is general and admits specification. Also, it is possible that the intended meaning is to urge the sinners to repentance and return to God, and not to despair of God's mercy due to committing sin so that it would prevent them from repentance. This is indicated by His saying, the Exalted, after this verse: 'And turn to your Lord and submit to Him...' [al-Zumar 39:54].
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Murji'ah doctrine on punishment. First, it states the doctrine: punishment is only fitting for disbelievers, not Muslims, and those who die with major sins without repentance will not be punished. Then it lists their proofs from the Quran: verses that mention disgrace and punishment specifically for disbelievers (16:27, 3:192, 20:48, 67:8, 92:15-16, 34:17), a verse that might seem to threaten all (4:123) but they claim it is outweighed by mercy, and verses that seem to promise mercy to believers (3:106, 80:38, 39:53). The author then provides the answer: the verses specifying punishment for disbelievers refer to eternal punishment, which is indeed specific to them, while verses like 39:53 are general and can be specified to urge repentance, as indicated by the following verse (39:54). The passage thus defends the Sunni position that Muslim sinners may be punished temporarily but not eternally.

Key Terms
الخلود
التوبة
التخصيص
الوعد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Murji'ah believe that mercy verses guarantee forgiveness for Muslim sinners without repentance.
Correction: The verses are general and intended to encourage repentance, as shown by the immediate call to turn to Allah in the following verse.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, what is the intended meaning of the verse 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of God'?
A) That all sinners will be forgiven without condition
B) That disbelievers are also included
C) To urge sinners to repentance, as indicated by the next verse
D) That only believers can be forgiven

Key Takeaway
The Sunni refutation clarifies that punishment verses refer to eternal punishment for disbelievers, while mercy verses encourage repentance for believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you currently relying on verses like 'Do not despair of the mercy of Allah' to feel safe in a sin you have not repented from? What step will you take today to actually repent and return to Allah?
?
When you read the mercy verse, does it lead you to repent or to feel complacent? Which response does the context of the following verse demand from you right now?
?
The Murji'ah argued that mercy verses prove all sinners are forgiven. Could it be that you have unknowingly absorbed part of this mindset, treating repentance as optional? In what area of your life are you most at risk of this? Commit to changing it right now.

Response to the Objection from Verses of Threat
Sanusi refutes objections from Qur'anic verses of threat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi resolves apparent contradictions between verses of promise and threat by prioritizing God's mercy and specifying punishment for disbelievers.

Core Idea
God's mercy outweighs threats; punishment verses target only disbelievers.

Sanusi now confronts an objection from scriptural verses that seem to promise punishment for evil deeds. He shows that when promise and threat appear to conflict, the promise must prevail because God's mercy is more abundant. Then he explains that threatening verses actually refer to a specific, eternal punishment reserved for disbelievers, not for believing sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its literal translation. Note the objection and the multiple answers Sanusi provides.
The passage contains several Qur'anic citations.
2
Understand the first answer: precedence of promise
Sanusi's first move is to establish a rule: when promise and threat verses conflict, the promise is given precedence because God's mercy and bounty are more prevalent.
This is a key principle in kalam.
3
Examine the cited verses
Look at the three verses Sanusi cites: Al 'Imran 3:106, 'Abasa 80:38, and az-Zumar 39:53. Notice how each one is interpreted to support the idea that believers are not subject to eternal punishment.
The verse about 'faces becoming white and black' is taken to refer to the fate of believers vs. disbelievers.
4
Grasp the nuance about 'My servants'
The verse from az-Zumar is analyzed: it is general but can be specified. Sanusi proposes it urges repentance, not an unconditional promise. The following verse supports this interpretation.
This shows Sanusi's careful handling of scriptural evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لا يُقالُ : يعارضُهُ قولُهُ تعالى : مَن يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا يُجْزَ بِهِ ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲۳) لأنَّا نقول : يُرجحُ عندَ التعارض أي الوعد على آي الوعيد؛ لأنَّ رحمته تعالى وفضلَهُ أغلب و و وودرو وو وبقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ و يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوهٌ . . . [آل عمران : ١٠٦] الآية . وبقوله جلَّ وعزَّ : ﴿ وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَيذٍ تُسفِرَةٌ ﴾ [عبس: ٣٨] الآيةَ . وبقوله تعالى : ﴿ يَعِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ لَا تَقْنَطُوا مِن رَّحْمَةِ الله ... [الزمر : ٥٣] الآيةَ ، والمراد : المؤمنون؛ لأنَّ الإضافة تشعر بتشريف ما ، ولا شرفَ للكافر . : أنَّ الآياتِ المخصصة العذابَ بالكافر والجواب عن الجميع مرادُها عذابٌ وخزي خاص، وهو الذي يقتضي الخلود، ولا فلاح بعدَهُ والعياذُ باللهِ، ولا خفاءَ أَنَّ ذلك خاص بالكافِرِ . وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ يَعِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ * فهو عام يقبلُ التخصيص، وأيضاً : فيحتملُ أنَّ المراد حضُّ العصاة على التوبة والرجوع إلى الله تعالى، وألا يقنطوا بمواقعة الذنبِ مِنْ رحمة الله تعالى حتى يصدَّهم ذلك عن التوبة، ويدلُّ عليه قوله تعالى إثْرَ هذهِ الآية : ﴿ وَأَنبُوا إِلَى رَبِّكُمْ وَأَسْلِمُوا لَهُ ... [الزمر : ٥٤] الآيةَ
And it is not said: It is contradicted by His statement, the Exalted: 'Whoever does evil will be recompensed for it' [an-Nisa 4:123]; because we say: In case of contradiction, the promise is given precedence over the verses of threat, because His mercy, the Exalted, and His bounty are more prevalent. And [?] and by His statement, the Exalted: 'On the Day when faces become white and faces become black' [Al 'Imran 3:106] the verse. And by His statement, the Mighty and Majestic: 'Faces on that Day will be bright' ['Abasa 80:38] the verse. And by His statement, the Exalted: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of God' [az-Zumar 39:53] the verse; and the intended are the believers, because the possessive construction suggests some honor, and there is no honor for the disbeliever. That the verses specify punishment for the disbeliever. And the answer about all of them: their intended meaning is a specific punishment and disgrace, which necessitates everlastingness, and there is no success after it, and God forbid, and it is not hidden that that is specific to the disbeliever. As for His statement, the Exalted: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves' it is general and admits specification, and also: it is possible that the intended meaning is to urge the disobedient to repentance and return to God, the Exalted, and that they should not despair due to committing sin from the mercy of God, the Exalted, lest that prevent them from repentance, and it is indicated by His statement, the Exalted, after this verse: 'And turn in repentance to your Lord and surrender to Him' [az-Zumar 39:54] the verse.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. Sanusi presents an objection that might be raised by those who argue that Qur'anic verses promising punishment for evil deeds contradict the claim that only disbelievers are eternally punished. He then gives multiple answers. First, he states that when there is a contradiction between verses of promise (wa'd) and verses of threat (wa'id), the promise is given precedence because God's mercy and bounty predominate. He then cites three verses that seem to show believers being rewarded or saved: the verse about faces becoming white and black (Al 'Imran 3:106), the verse about faces being bright ('Abasa 80:38), and the verse calling on those who have transgressed not to despair of God's mercy (az-Zumar 39:53). He explains that the latter specifically addresses believers because the possessive 'My servants' indicates honor, which disbelievers do not have. Then he summarizes that all these verses refer to a specific punishment and disgrace that entails everlastingness, and that is clearly only for disbelievers. Finally, he addresses the verse from az-Zumar more thoroughly: it is general and can be specified, and it is likely meant to urge sinners to repent and not be prevented from repentance by despair. This is supported by the following verse that commands turning to God and submission.

آيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that verses threatening punishment apply to all sinners, including believers, implying that believers can be eternally punished for sins.
Correction: Sanusi shows that such verses are either overridden by God's predominant mercy, or they refer specifically to disbelievers, or they are meant to encourage repentance, not to threaten eternal punishment for believers.

B) Because God's mercy and bounty predominate.
C) Because verses of threat are abrogated.
D) Because the Qur'an explicitly commands it.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi argues that verses of threat are limited to disbelievers, and God's mercy takes precedence, ensuring believers are not eternally punished.

?

?
The passage teaches that God's mercy outweighs His threat. If you truly believed that, how would it change the way you treat yourself and others when mistakes are made? Is there a person you have judged harshly because you forgot this truth?

The Third School: Punishment and Classification of People
Third school and Ahl al-Sunna taxonomy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third madhhab on punishment and the Ahl al-Sunna classification of people's fate.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna: punishment for believers is by revelation, not eternal, and not for all sinners.

Having presented the first two madhhabs, Sanusi now explains the third school, which affirms punishment for both disbelievers and sinful believers. He clarifies the distinct basis for this in Ahl al-Sunna vs. Mu'tazila, and then provides a comprehensive taxonomy of human destiny according to Ahl al-Sunna. This passage establishes the nuanced view that while disbelievers are eternally punished, believers who sin may be forgiven or punished temporarily.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the conciseness of Sanusi's style and the logical flow from the third school to the classification.
2
Identify the third school and its basis
Locate the claim of the third school and note how Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila agree on punishment being good but differ on its source (revelation vs. reason).
This is a key distinction in Islamic theology.
3
Understand the disagreements
Sanusi points out two disagreements: (1) punishment for sinful believers is not eternal according to Ahl al-Sunna, and (2) it is not comprehensive because God forgives many. The Mu'tazila opposed both.
This shows the more merciful stance of Ahl al-Sunna.
4
Trace the classification of people
Follow the taxonomy from people divided into believers and disbelievers, then believers into preserved and not preserved, then into minor sinners and major sinners, and finally into repentant and unrepentant. Note the ultimate destination for each group.
This classification is foundational for understanding Ahl al-Sunna eschatology.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this classification balances divine justice and mercy. The possibility of forgiveness and temporary punishment for believers emphasizes God's mercy, while eternal punishment for disbelievers underscores justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذهب الثالثُ : أنَّ العذابَ ثابت حسن في حق الكفار وعصاةِ المؤمنين ، وهذا هو الذي أجمعَ عليهِ أهلُ السنَّةِ والمعتزلة ، إلا أنَّ حسْنَهُ عند أهل السنَّةِ بالشرع ، وعند المعتزلة بالعقل ، وأيضاً : فليس دائماً هو في حقٌّ مَنْ نفذَ فِيهِ مِنْ عصاة المؤمنين عند أهل السنة ولا شاملاً عندَهم لجميع العصاةِ ؛ لثبوتِ عفوه تعالى عن كثير . وخالف المعتزلة في الأمرين . وبالجملة : فمذهب جميع أهلِ الحقِّ وأهل السنَّةِ : أنَّ الناس على قسمين : مؤمن وكافر ؛ فالكافر في النارِ مُخلَّدٌ فيها بإجماع ، والمؤمن على ضربين : محفوظ مِنَ المعاصي عمره وغيرُ محفوظ ؛ فالأوَّلُ : في الجنةِ بَدْءاً بالإجماع ، والثاني : صاحب صغائر وصاحب كبائر ، وصاحبُ الكبائر : تائب وغير تائب ، فالقسمان الأولان أيضاً في الجنَّةِ أبداً بالإجماع ، وربَّما تكون بعد أهوال ثم
The third school: that punishment is established and good for disbelievers and sinful believers alike, and this is what Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila have agreed upon, except that its being good is for Ahl al-Sunna by revelation, and for the Mu'tazila by reason. And also: it is not perpetual for those of the sinful believers upon whom it is executed according to Ahl al-Sunna, nor is it comprehensive according to them for all sinners, because of the establishment of His forgiveness, the Exalted, for many. The Mu'tazila disagreed in both matters. And in summary: the school of all the people of truth and Ahl al-Sunna is that people are of two kinds: believer and disbeliever. The disbeliever is in the Fire, eternally therein by consensus. The believer is of two types: one preserved from sins throughout his life, and one not preserved. The first is in Paradise from the beginning by consensus. The second is one who commits minor sins and one who commits major sins. The one who commits major sins: the repentant and the unrepentant. The first two categories [the preserved from sin and the repentant major sinner] are also in Paradise forever by consensus, and perhaps after terrors, then...
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the third theological school (madhhab) regarding punishment. Sanusi begins by stating that this school holds punishment to be established and good for both disbelievers and sinful believers. He notes that Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila agree on this point, but differ on the basis: for Ahl al-Sunna, the goodness of punishment is known by revelation (shar'), while for the Mu'tazila it is known by reason ('aql). He then clarifies the Ahl al-Sunna position further: punishment for sinful believers is neither eternal nor all-encompassing; it is not perpetual because many are forgiven, and it is not for every sinner because God's forgiveness covers many. The Mu'tazila opposed Ahl al-Sunna on both points (i.e., they held punishment to be eternal and all-encompassing for all unrepentant sinners). Sanusi then summarizes the complete taxonomy of human destiny according to Ahl al-Sunna: people are either believers or disbelievers; disbelievers are eternally in Hell by consensus; believers are either those protected from sin all their lives (who go straight to Paradise by consensus) or those who are not protected. The latter are further divided into those who commit minor sins and those who commit major sins. Among major sinners, some repent and some do not. The first two categories (the protected and the repentant major sinner) are in Paradise forever, though the repentant may experience some terrors before entering. The passage ends incompletely with 'then', indicating the discussion likely continues on the next page.

أهل السنة
المعتزلة

العقل

الخلود
العصاة
الكبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Ahl al-Sunna believe all sinners, including believers, will be eternally punished.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that punishment for believers is not eternal and not all-encompassing due to God’s forgiveness.

Checkpoint
On what basis do Ahl al-Sunna hold that punishment is good for disbelievers and sinful believers, according to Sanusi?
A) By reason alone.
B) By revelation (shar').
C) By consensus.
D) By both reason and revelation.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna teaches that punishment for believers is neither eternal nor all-encompassing; the ultimate fate depends on faith, repentance, and divine mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
According to the classification in this passage, you are either among the believers preserved from sin (maḥfūẓ) or among those who commit sins (minor or major). Honestly, if you died tonight, which category would you fall into? What does your answer reveal about your current relationship with sin and repentance?
?
The passage states that punishment for sinful believers is not eternal because God has established His forgiveness for many. Have you ever taken God's mercy for granted, assuming you can sin without consequence? What specific sin do you need to repent from today, not just in words but with a firm resolve to change?
?
The Mu'tazila believe that punishment for sinful believers is perpetual and all-encompassing, while Ahl al-Sunna believe it is limited and many are forgiven. Which view truly humbles you? If you rely on reason alone, what would you deserve? But if you rely on God's revelation and mercy, how should that change the way you live right now?

The Prophet's Intercession for Sinful Believers
Sanusi affirms the Prophet's intercession and refutes Mu'tazila denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH) intercedes for sinful believers and why the Mu'tazila rejected this.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession saves sinful believers from eternal punishment.

This passage from Sanusi's work affirms a key Sunni belief: that the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH) will intercede for sinful Muslims to remove them from Hellfire. This directly opposes the Mu'tazila view that grave sinners are eternally punished. Let's examine the source text and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi begins with a general statement about forgiveness before focusing on intercession.
2
Identify the two key affirmations
The passage first states that forgiveness of non-repentant sinners is in Allah's will, with consensus that some will be punished. Then it affirms the Prophet's intercession for sinful believers. Find these two points.
The second point is the main focus of this lesson.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
The Mu'tazila denied intercession based on their principle that a grave sinner (fasiq) is eternally in Hell like a disbeliever. Ask yourself why this principle leads to rejection of intercession.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يغفر الله سبحانه، وغير التائب في مشيئة الله تعالى، مع إجماعهم على نفوذ الوعيد في بعضهم؛ وهو جماعة من كل نوع من أنواع المعاصي وأما شفاعة سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في إخراج عصاة المؤمنين من النار: فلا خفاء في ثبوتها عند أهل السنة، وأنكرها المعتزلة على أصلهم في أن الفاسق مخلد في النار كالكافر، ولنبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم شفاعات أخر مشهورة في كتب الحديث، نسأله سبحانه ألا يحرمنا منها
Allah Glorified forgives, and other than the repentant is in the will of Allah Most High, with their consensus on the execution of the threat (of punishment) upon some of them; and they are a group from every type of types of sins. And as for the intercession of our Master and Patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in bringing out sinful believers from the Fire: there is no obscurity in its establishment among the People of the Sunna, and the Mu'tazila denied it based on their principle that the immoral person is eternally in the Fire like the disbeliever. And for our Prophet and Patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, there are other well-known intercessions in the books of hadith. We ask Him Glorified not to deprive us of them.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage affirms two doctrines: that forgiveness of sins for non-repentant sinners is subject to Allah's will, but there is consensus that some sinners will indeed face punishment. Then it specifically affirms the intercession of the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH) to remove sinful believers from Hellfire, which is a firmly established Sunni creed. The Mu'tazila denied this because they held that a grave sinner (fasiq) becomes an eternal inhabitant of Hell like a disbeliever, leaving no room for intercession. The author also notes that there are other well-known intercessions of the Prophet mentioned in hadith collections, and prays to benefit from them.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
عصاة المؤمنين
الفاسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believed grave sinners (fasiq) are eternally in Hell like disbelievers, so no intercession can remove them.
Correction: Sunni belief holds that the Prophet's intercession can remove sinful believers from Hell, and their punishment is not eternal.

Checkpoint
Why did the Mu'tazila deny the Prophet's intercession for sinful believers?
A) They believed the Prophet could not intercede for anyone.
B) They held that the grave sinner (fasiq) is eternally in Hell like a disbeliever.
C) They denied the existence of Hellfire altogether.
D) They claimed intercession is only for prophets themselves.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad's intercession for sinful believers is a fundamental Sunni doctrine, rejected by Mu'tazila due to their view of eternal punishment for grave sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own sins, do you rely more on your own efforts to be 'good enough' or on the hope of the Prophet's intercession? Which attitude does this lesson challenge you to adopt?
?
If the Mu'tazila were right that a single grave sin makes you eternally doomed like a disbeliever, how would your life change right now? What does the Sunni doctrine of intercession allow you to do differently today?
?
The text mentions 'other intercessions' of the Prophet that are well-known. Have you ever sincerely asked the Prophet to intercede for you in your prayers? If not, what is holding you back from seeking this gift that Allah has granted?
